			Azimuth&A component of an MLS consisting of an SHF transmitter and associated equipment, radiating signals in a volume of airspace served by the MLS, thereby furnishing azimuth indications to aircraft approaching the runway or back azimuth indications to aircraft departing from the runway or performing a missed ApproachProcedure.

Azimuth-type&A code indicating if it is 'normal' or 'back' azimuth equipment.
Azimuth-trueBearing&The measured angle between the azimuth beam and True North at the azimuth antenna.
Azimuth-trueBearingAccuracy&Accuracy of the measured angle between the azimuth beam and True North at the azimuth antenna
Azimuth-magneticBearing&The measured angle between the direction of the azimuth beam and Magnetic North at the azimuth antenna.
Azimuth-angleProportionalLeft&The value of the angle within which the azimuth indication is proportional to the deviation from the azimuth zero indication direction, and left of this direction from the azimuth antenna.
Azimuth-angleProportionalRight&The value of the angle within which the azimuth indication is proportional to the deviation from the azimuth zero indication direction, and right of this direction from the azimuth antenna.
Azimuth-angleCoverLeft&The value of the angle from the zero indication direction within which the azimuth indication is usable, and left of this direction from the azimuth antenna.
Azimuth-angleCoverRight&The value of the angle from the zero indication direction within which the azimuth indication is usable, and right of this direction from the azimuth antenna.
Azimuth-channel&A code indicating the channel on which the Microwave Landing System is operating.

			CheckpointINS&A point established to test the Inertial Navigation System in the aircraft.


			CheckpointVOR&A VOR test transmits a test signal used to determine the accuracy of a VOR receiver on the ground or airborne.


			DME&Ultra High Frequency (UHF) ground equipment that is used in conjunction with airborne equipment to determine distance between the airborne and ground equipment.

DME-type&The particular spectrum characteristics or accuracy of Ultra High Frequency (UHF) Distance Measuring Equipment (DME), as a category.
DME-channel&The channel of the DME.
See Annex 10, Table A, end of Chapter 3 for channelling details and for a list of allowable values.
DME-ghostFrequency&The frequency of a virtual VHF facility paired with the DME according to ICAO Annex 10, table A, ch.3.
DME-displace&The distance from the DME antenna to the position where the zero range indication occurs in the DME receiver.

			DirectionFinder&An electronic device used to determine the position of a radio source by means of directional antennas, which receives the strongest radio signal when it is pointing directly at the transmitter.

DirectionFinder-doppler&Indicates whether the equipment uses the Doppler effect for higher precision.

			Elevation&A component of an MLS consisting of an SHF transmitter, and associated equipment radiating signals within a volume of airspace served by the MLS, thereby furnishing elevation information as an angular value to aircraft approaching the runway.

Elevation-angleNominal&The normal glide path angle for the MLS installation.
Elevation-angleMinimum&The value of the lowest elevation angle authorized for an MLS procedure.
Elevation-angleSpan&The value of the span angle of the elevation transmitter signal between the lower and the upper limits.
Elevation-angleAccuracy&Accuracy of the elevation angle.

			Glidepath&A component of an ILS consisting of a UHF transmitter radiating signals and providing a straight line descent path in the vertical plane containing the centre line of the runway served by the ILS, and thereby furnishing descent information down to the lowest authorized decision height or to the surface of a runway, depending on the Facility Performance Category of the ILS.

Glidepath-frequency&The frequency value of the glide path indicator.
Glidepath-slope&The angle of the glide path.
Glidepath-angleAccuracy&Accuracy of the Glide path angle.
Glidepath-rdh&The value of the ILS Reference Datum Height (ILS RDH).
Glidepath-rdhAccuracy&Accuracy of the value of the ILS Reference Datum Height (ILS RDH).

			Localizer&A component of an ILS consisting of a VHF transmitter, radiating signals in the direction served by the ILS, to provide a straight line descent path in the vertical plane containing the centre line of the runway.

Localizer-frequency&The frequency of the localizer.
Localizer-magneticBearing&The measured angle between the localizer beam and Magnetic North at the localizer antenna.
Localizer-magneticBearingAccuracy&Accuracy of the measured angle between the localizer beam and Magnetic North at the localizer antenna.
Localizer-trueBearing&The measured angle between the localizer beam and True North at the localizer antenna. Note : The True North is the north point at which the meridian lines meet.
Localizer-trueBearingAccuracy&Accuracy of the measured angle between the localizer beam and True North at the localizer antenna. 
Localizer-declination&The angular difference between True North and the station declination (Magnetic North - as indicated by the station).
Localizer-widthCourse&The localizer course width, in degrees.
Localizer-widthCourseAccuracy&Accuracy of the localizer course width, in degrees.
Localizer-backCourseUsable&A code indicating the usability of the localizer signal in the back course sector.

			MarkerBeacon&A marker beacon serving to identify a particular location in space by means of a 75MHz transmitter which transmits a directional signal to be received by aircraft flying overhead.

MarkerBeacon-class&A code indicating the class of the radio marker.
For example, fan marker, low-powered fan marker, Z marker.
MarkerBeacon-frequency&The value of the radio emission frequency.
MarkerBeacon-axisBearing&The true bearing of the minor axis of the marker beacon.
(source: ARINC 424 Specification)
MarkerBeacon-auralMorseCode&The Morse code transmitted by the beacon.

			NDB&A Non-directional radio beacon. A low or medium frequency radio beacon which transmits signals whereby the pilot of an aircraft properly equipped can determine bearings and 'home in' on the station.

NDB-frequency&The frequency of the NDB emission.
NDB-class&The class of the NDB.
For example, NDB or Locator.
NDB-emissionBand&The emission band for the NDB

			Navaid&A service providing guidance information or position data for the efficient and safe operation of aircraft supported by one or more radio navigation aids.

Navaid-type&Type of the navaid service such as ILS, MLS, VORTAC, VOR/DME, etc.
Navaid-designator&The coded identifier given to the navaid system.
Navaid-name&The long name given to the composite navaid.
Navaid-flightChecked&Indicates if the navaid has been flight checked.
Navaid-purpose&Indication of the intended usage of the navaid (enroute or terminal)
Navaid-signalPerformance&The signal performance level indicating the precision of an ILS or MLS system.
Navaid-courseQuality&An indication of the signal quality of the ILS course structure based on the location the precision signal is usable to.
Navaid-integrityLevel&That quality which relates to the trust which can be placed in the correctness of the information supplied by the ILS facility.

			NavaidComponent&Indicates navigation use of a NavaidEquipment as a component of the navigation service provided by a Navaid. 

For example the DME NavaidEquipment is a NavaidComponent of an ILS system.  The DME may be collocated with the Localizer and the DME may provide the navigable location for the Navaid service.

NavaidComponent-collocationGroup&Set of navaid equipments that are collocated.  All Navaid equipment that has the same value for this property are collocated together.  For example in a VOR/DME Navaid the VOR and DME navaid equipment will be assigned the same collocationGroup number = 1.  For example an ILS might have a Localizer with collocation Group number = 1 and collocated DME and Glidepath sharing collocationGroup number = 2.  
NavaidComponent-markerPosition&A code indicating the position, in a navaid landing system, of the markers situated on the centreline of a runway. For example:  outer, middle, etc..
NavaidComponent-providesNavigableLocation&Indicates the navaid equipment used to specify the navigable location of the Navaid when the navaid is used as significant point

			NavaidEquipment&A physical navaid equipment like VOR, DME, localizer, TACAN, etc..

NavaidEquipment-designator&The identifying code given to the navaid.
NavaidEquipment-name&The long name given to the navaid equipment.
NavaidEquipment-emissionClass&A code indicating the type of emission, as defined at the 1979 ITU World Administrative Radio Conference.
NavaidEquipment-mobile&Indicates if the navaid equipment is mobile.
NavaidEquipment-magneticVariation&The measured angle between Magnetic North and True North at the VOR and at the time reported in dateMagneticVariation. By convention, the measure is expressed as a positive number if Magnetic North is to the east of True North and negative if Magnetic North is to the west of True North. Therefore, magnetic bearing + magnetic variation = true bearing. The following rule of thumb applies: ""variation east-magnetic least, variation west-magnetic best"".
NavaidEquipment-magneticVariationAccuracy&The accuracy of the measured angle between Magnetic North and True North at the VOR and at the time reported in dateMagneticVariation
NavaidEquipment-dateMagneticVariation&The year the magnetic variation was measured.
NavaidEquipment-flightChecked&Indicates if the navaid equipment has been flight checked.

			NavaidEquipmentMonitoring&Navaid equipment monitoring information.

NavaidEquipmentMonitoring-monitored&Navaid equipment is monitored or not.

			NavaidOperationalStatus&Navaid operational status information.

NavaidOperationalStatus-operationalStatus&Indicates the state of the navaid.
NavaidOperationalStatus-signalType&The type of signal that is affected by the operational status.

			NavigationSystemCheckpoint&A point established and marked on the surface of an aerodrome allowing the checking of a navigation system (like VOR, GNSS, etc.) or initialisation of an inertial navigation system.

NavigationSystemCheckpoint-category&Indicates the position of the checkpoint; airborne or ground
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-upperLimit&Indicating the upper limit of the block in which the check should be conducted.
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-upperLimitReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-lowerLimit&Indicating the lower limit of the block in which the check should be conducted.
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-lowerLimitReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-altitudeInterpretation&Indicates how the upper and/or lower altitude values should be interpreted.
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-distance&The value of the distance from the checkpoint to the navaid.
NavigationSystemCheckpoint-angle&The indication of a bearing (at a given point) by the measurement of the angle between the checkpoint and the navaid equipment (VOR)

			SDF&Simplified Directional Facility (SDF)  provides a final approach course similar to that of the ILS localizer although is not as precise as Localizer. It does not provide glide slope information. 
The SDF transmits signals within the range of 108.10 to 111.95 MHz. 
The approach techniques and procedures used in an SDF instrument approach are essentially the same as those employed in executing a standard localizer approach except the SDF course may not be aligned with the runway and the course may be wider, resulting in less precision. 
Usable off-course indications are limited to 35 degrees either side of the course centreline. Instrument indications received beyond 35 degrees should be disregarded. 
This angle is generally not more than 3 degrees. 
The SDF signal is fixed at either 6 degrees or 12 degrees as necessary to provide maximum flyability and optimum course quality.

SDF-frequency&The frequency of the localizer.
SDF-magneticBearing&The measured angle between the localizer beam and Magnetic North at the localizer antenna.
SDF-trueBearing&The measured angle between the localizer beam and True North at the localizer antenna. Note : The True North is the north point at which the meridian lines meet.

			SpecialNavigationStation&A land based station of a special navigation system.

SpecialNavigationStation-name&The textual name of the station.
SpecialNavigationStation-type&A code indicating the type of service within the chain.
E.g. Master, Red Slave (DECCA), Slave (LORAN) etc..
SpecialNavigationStation-frequency&The value of the emission frequency.
SpecialNavigationStation-emission&A code indicating the type of emission, as defined at the 1979 ITU World Administrative Radio Conference.

			SpecialNavigationStationStatus&Special Navigation Station Status information.

SpecialNavigationStationStatus-operationalStatus&Operational status.

			SpecialNavigationSystem&A wide area (worldwide) navigation system based on a chain of land stations or a satellite constellation providing radio frequency signals which can be used by airborne equipment to determine at least, the aircrafts two-dimensional position or, depending on the capability of the system, the three-dimensional position.

SpecialNavigationSystem-type&A code indicating the type of special navigation system.
For example, LORAN, DECCA, GNSS, etc.
SpecialNavigationSystem-designator&The designator (coded identifier) of a special navigation system chain.
SpecialNavigationSystem-name&The textual name of the chain of a special navigation system.
For example, Mangern Chain

			TACAN&A UHF Tactical Air Navigation beacon. A navigation system developed by military and naval forces providing, as far as the navigating pilot is concerned and for suitably equipped aircraft, the same indication as a VOR/DME system.

TACAN-channel&A code indicating the channel of the TACAN system.
TACAN-declination&The angular difference between the direction of the 'zero bearing' indicated by the station and the direction of the True North.

			VOR&A VHF omnidirectional radio range beacon. A short-range, very-high-frequency omnidirectional beacon which provides an indication in the aircraft of the bearing of the beacon, or left-right track indication.

VOR-type&A code indicating a type of VOR, e.g. conventional VOR or Doppler VOR.
VOR-frequency&The value of the frequency.
VOR-zeroBearingDirection&A code indicating the direction of the 'zero bearing' provided by the station. For example: magnetic north, true north.
VOR-declination&The angular difference between True North and the station declination (Magnetic North - as indicated by the station).

			
			AngleIndication&An angular reference from a navaid or with reference to a designated point.

AngleIndication-angle&The indication of a bearing (at a given point) by the measurement of the angle between the bearing and either True North or Magnetic North (this should appear explicitly or implicitly). The angle is measured clockwise from 0 degrees up to but not including 360 degrees. The value can also be a VOR radial.
For example, Westward is expressed as 270.
AngleIndication-angleType&A code indicating the direction of the zero bearing.  For example, magnetic north or true north.
AngleIndication-indicationDirection&Code indicating the if the angle is TO or FROM the Navaid or Designated Point that is used.
AngleIndication-trueAngle&The indication of a bearing (at a given point) by the measurement of the angle between the bearing and True North.  The angle is measured clockwise from 0 degrees up to but not including 360 degrees. The value can also be a VOR radial.
For example, Westward is expressed as 270.
AngleIndication-cardinalDirection&The angle expressed as compass direction.  
AngleIndication-minimumReceptionAltitude&The lowest altitude that an aircraft can receive signal.

			AngleUse&Indicates the role of the AngleIndication in the PointReference (for example, along track versus intersecting).

AngleUse-alongCourseGuidance&Defines if the angle indication provides the course guidance for the segment.

			DistanceIndication&A distance reference from a navaid or with reference to a designated point.

DistanceIndication-distance&The value of the distance.
DistanceIndication-minimumReceptionAltitude&The lowest altitude that an aircraft can receive signal.
DistanceIndication-type&indicates the distance is from distance measuring equipment or just a simple distance

			EnRouteSegmentPoint&Indicates a point associated with a defined  EnRoute segment.  

EnRouteSegmentPoint-roleFreeFlight&Free flight is a an air traffic control method that uses no centralized control (e.g. air traffic controllers). Instead, parts of airspace are reserved dynamically and automatically in a distributed way using computer communication to ensure the required separation between aircraft
EnRouteSegmentPoint-roleRVSM&A code indicating that the point has a specific role in the reduced vertical separation minima (RVSM) context.
EnRouteSegmentPoint-turnRadius&The recommended turn radius when continuing on the previous segment of the route (start point) or when continuing on the next segment of the route(end point). 
EnRouteSegmentPoint-roleMilitaryTraining&A code indicating the usage of the point in the case of a military training route.

			PointReference&Defines the location of a designated point using a combination of angles and distances based on the GuidanceService.  The set of angles and distances must not under specify the location.

The indications that are part of the PointReference must locate the same designated point.

PointReference-role&Describes the role of the defined PointReference. Example: DME,  INT, recommended navaid, fix tolerance  
PointReference-priorFixTolerance&Because the fix may be received early, protection against obstacles must be provided from a line perpendicular to the flight course.  PriorFixTolerance indicates the error distance (from the fix to the earliest point where the fix may be received along the flight course.
PointReference-postFixTolerance&Indicates the error distance (from the fix to the latest point where the fix may be received along the flight course.  

			SegmentPoint&Indicates a point associated with a defined segment.  

SegmentPoint-reportingATC&Indicating the type of position report required by an ATC Unit.  Eg.: compulsory or on request. 
SegmentPoint-flyOver&Indicates if the aircraft is required to fly directly over the fix. If code is Yes, then it is a 'fly-over' waypoint. If the code is No, then the associated fix is a 'fly-by' waypoint. [ICAO] Waypoints are identified as either flyover or fly-by.

Fly-by waypoint. A waypoint which requires turn anticipation to allow tangential interception of the next segment of a route or procedure

Flyover waypoint. A waypoint at which a turn is initiated in order to join the next segment of a route or procedure.
SegmentPoint-waypoint&A point used for RNAV procedures/routes.
SegmentPoint-radarGuidance&Radar guidance is possible for reaching this point.

			TerminalSegmentPoint&Indicates a point or a condition associated with a defined SegmentLeg.  

TerminalSegmentPoint-role&Identifies the function or position the point plays in the ApproachProcedure.
TerminalSegmentPoint-leadRadial&The lead radial provides information for aircraft with single receiving equipment to change the receiver to the localizer or other facility providing the course guidance and to ensure the aircraft is within the clearance coverage area of LOC facilities before changing frequency or accepting on-course indication.
TerminalSegmentPoint-leadDME&The lead DME , like the lead Radial, provides information for aircraft with single receiving equipment to change the receiver to the localizer or other facility providing the course guidance and to ensure the aircraft is within the clearance coverage area of LOC facilities before changing frequency or accepting on-course indication.
TerminalSegmentPoint-indicatorFACF&Indicates the point is also a Final Approach Course Fix (FACF).

			
			DesignatedPoint&A  geographical location not marked by the site of a radio navigation aid, used in defining an ATS route, the flight path of an aircraft or for other navigation or ATS purposes.

DesignatedPoint-designator&The coded designator of the point.
For example, the five-letter ICAO name of the point, etc..
DesignatedPoint-type&The kind of point designator, indicating the rules by which the designator has been created.
DesignatedPoint-name&The full textual name of a designated point, if any.
For example, 'GOTAN Intersection' for GOTAN. Name may also be used to identify an unnamed point (See ARINC 424 for unnamed points.

			SignificantPoint&A link class that allows selecting between a navaid system, a runway point, an airport reference point, an aiming point or a fix designated point.
SignificantPoint accounts for a specified geographical location used to define an ATS route, the flight path of an aircraft or for other navigation/ATS purposes.


			SignificantPointInAirspace&A significant point's use and relative location to an airspace.

SignificantPointInAirspace-type&A code indicating the way a significant point is used in association to airspace.
Description:
Ex: entry point, exit point, etc.
SignificantPointInAirspace-relativeLocation&A code indicating the location of a significant point in relation to airspace.
Description:
Ex: In, Out, On Border.

			
			AeronauticalGroundLight&A light specifically provided as an aid to air navigation, with the exception of obstacle lights and lights forming part of surface or approach lighting systems

AeronauticalGroundLight-name&The name by which the ground light is known
AeronauticalGroundLight-type&A classification of the light based on the kind of item that it visually identifies
AeronauticalGroundLight-colour&The primary colour of the light source.
AeronauticalGroundLight-flashing&An indication whether the light is steady or flashing.

			
			LinguisticNote&The note content expressed in a specific language. As a minimum, all Notes shall be expressed in English.

LinguisticNote-note&The text of the Note, in a specific language.

			Note&A general text note for a feature or for one of its properties.

Note-propertyName&The name of the feature property for which this note is relevant, if applicable. If no propertyName is specified, then the Note is relevant for the feature as a whole.
Note-purpose&An indication of the goal which led to the provision of the free text note.

			
			ObstacleArea&An area defined by ICAO for the purpose of collecting obstacle data in electronic format, as necessary to satisfy requirements of air navigation systems or functions.

ObstacleArea-type&Indicates the type of the obstacle coverage area. Examples: Area 1, 2, 3 or 4.
ObstacleArea-obstructionIdSurfaceCondition&Obstruction identification surface that obstructing area represents

			ObstacleAreaOrigin&A link class that allows selecting the feature for which the Obstacle Area has been defined


			VerticalStructure&All fixed (whether temporary or permanent) and mobile objects, or parts thereof that extend above the surface of the Earth. Those vertical structures that are located on an area intended for the surface movement of aircraft or that extend above a defined surface intended to protect aircraft in flight are considered obstacles.

VerticalStructure-name&The name of the vertical structure, if applicable,
VerticalStructure-type&A code indicating the type of vertical structure, such as building, tower, cable, etc.
VerticalStructure-lighted&A simple indication that the obstacle is lighted, when no further details are available.
VerticalStructure-markingICAOStandard&Indicates if the markings comply with the ICAO standard, as described in Annex 14.
VerticalStructure-group&A flag indicating whether the vertical structure consists of a number of closely situated similar objects.
VerticalStructure-length&Overall length of the obstruction
VerticalStructure-width&Overall width of the obstruction
VerticalStructure-radius&The overall radius of an obstacle that has a relatively circular shape
VerticalStructure-lightingICAOStandard&Indicates if the lighting is ICAO standard as described in Annex 14.
VerticalStructure-synchronisedLighting&Indicates that the flashing LightElements that compose the lighting of the vertical structure (could be a group) are synchronised (flash in unison).

			VerticalStructureLightingStatus&The description of the operational status of the Vertical Structure lighting.

VerticalStructureLightingStatus-status&A code indicating the operational status of the lighting. For example, serviceable, unserviceable, work in progress, etc.

			VerticalStructurePart&A part of the vertical structure that can be represented as point, line or polygon with vertical extent.

VerticalStructurePart-verticalExtent&The extent of the vertical structure part.
VerticalStructurePart-verticalExtentAccuracy&Accuracy of the value of the declared vertical extent.
VerticalStructurePart-type&A code indicating the type of vertical structure, such as building, tower, cable, etc.
VerticalStructurePart-constructionStatus&This property enables the provision of information about the construction of the man-made object that constitutes the vertical structure.
VerticalStructurePart-markingPattern&The general layout of the external paint or another marking element, intended to increase the visibility of the vertical structure.
VerticalStructurePart-markingFirstColour&The principal colour of the marking.
VerticalStructurePart-markingSecondColour&The secondary colour for the marking.
VerticalStructurePart-mobile&A flag indicating whether the vertical structure is expected to move around its nominal location. The accuracy property of the related Point, Surface or Point can be used to provide the maximum displacement range.
VerticalStructurePart-frangible&Boolean indicating whether the obstruction is easily broken
VerticalStructurePart-visibleMaterial&The type(s) of material that compose the load-bearing structure and/or exterior facing of a vertical construction (for example: a building or non-building structure).
VerticalStructurePart-designator&An alphanumeric code by which the structure is identified locally.

			VerticalStructurePartGeometry&A link class that allows selecting between the three different possibilities for describing the horizontal projection of an obstacle: point, line or polygon


			
			OrganisationAuthority&A feature used to model various Organisations and Authorities. For example: ATS Organisations, Aircraft Operating Agencies, States, Groups of States, etc.

OrganisationAuthority-name&The full official name of the State, Organisation, Authority, aircraft operating agency, handling agency etc.

Description:
CA= Canada, FAA= Federal Aviation Administration,  UK = United Kingdom, ICAO = International Civil Aviation Organization

OrganisationAuthority-military&Information on the type of operations allowed.

			OrganisationAuthorityAssociation&This entity type serves to realise the different 'two-way associations' which may exist between 'organisations/authorities' of the same and/or different types.
Example:
- an organisation/authority/agency may consist of any number of other organisations/authorities/agencies;

OrganisationAuthorityAssociation-type&The kind of association between two Organisations/Authorities.

			Unit&A generic term meaning variously all types of 'units' providing all types of services. This includes particularly Air Traffic Management (ATM) Units but also units which are not express verbs included in ATM such as SAR, MET, COM etc.

Unit-name&The full textual name of a unit. This name must be established according to the rules specified by ICAO, viz.: in the official language of the country, transposed into the Latin Alphabet where necessary.
Unit-type&A type by which the Unit is recognised, usually related to the standard type of services provided by it (e.g. area control centre, advisory centre, aeronautical information services office).
Unit-compliantICAO&A code indicating whether the Unit is setup according to the ICAO SARPS.
Unit-designator&A coded designator associated with the Unit. For example, the ICAO Location Indicator of an ACC, as listed in DOC 7910.
Unit-military&Indicates whether the Unit is civil, military or joint.

UnitAvailability-operationalStatus&Operational status information.

			UnitDependency&This association class describes the operational/functional relation that exists between a Unit and a RelatedUnit.

UnitDependency-type&The kind of dependency between the Unit and the RelatedUnit.

			
			
			
			ApproachAltitudeTable&Other altitudes (not defined by a segment) that are to be depicted on the profile view, such as HAT for ILS CAT II approaches.

ApproachAltitudeTable-measurementPoint&Indicates the point of the altitude measurement as reporting on a terminal procedure chart.
ApproachAltitudeTable-altitude&The calculated altitude at the indicated point.
ApproachAltitudeTable-altitudeReference&The reference for the altitude.

			ApproachCondition&The final approach condition that must be met to use the set of minima. For example, straight in approach to runway 9R Localizer only. (S-LOC 9R) (circling 8,16)

ApproachCondition-finalApproachPath&Enumerant indicating final approach path.
ApproachCondition-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.
ApproachCondition-climbGradient&The capability of an aircraft to climb with a certain gradient in take-off configuration.

			ApproachDistanceTable&Other distances (not defined by a segment) that are to be depicted on the profile view, such as HAT for ILS CAT II approaches.

ApproachDistanceTable-startingMeasurementPoint&Indicates starting point of the vertical or horizontal measurement

ApproachDistanceTable-endingMeasurementPoint&Indicates ending point of the vertical or horizontal measurement
ApproachDistanceTable-distance&Calculated distanced between the start and end point.

			ApproachTimingTable&Table of timings usually between final approach fix and the missed approach point.

ApproachTimingTable-startingMeasurementPoint&Indicates starting point of the vertical or horizontal measurement
ApproachTimingTable-endingMeasurementPoint&Indicates ending point of the vertical or horizontal measurement
ApproachTimingTable-time&The duration of the flight between the start point and the end point.
ApproachTimingTable-speed&The speed of the aircraft used to calculate the time.

			FinalProfile&The profile view of a final segment defined for an ApproachProcedure.


			InstrumentApproachProcedure&A series of predetermined manoeuvres by reference to flight instruments with specified protection from obstacles from the initial approach fix, or where applicable , from the beginning of a defined arrival route to a point from which a landing can be completed and thereafter, if a landing is not completed, to a position at which holding or en route obstacle clearance criteria apply.

InstrumentApproachProcedure-approachPrefix&Prefix used in support of current naming conventions
InstrumentApproachProcedure-approachType&A name describing the type of radio navigational aid/system
InstrumentApproachProcedure-multipleIdentification&One character code for multiple approaches of the same approach type; Z-A
InstrumentApproachProcedure-copterTrack&The final approach track value for copter procedures, 1 - 360.
InstrumentApproachProcedure-circlingIdentification&A suffix letter for circling only procedures, A - Z.
InstrumentApproachProcedure-courseReversalInstruction&Operational instructions that must be observed for procedure turns and tear drops.
InstrumentApproachProcedure-additionalEquipment&the additional equipment needed to fly the procedure not listed in approachType 
InstrumentApproachProcedure-channelGNSS&Operating channel of electronic transceiving equipment
InstrumentApproachProcedure-WAASReliable&Indicates an expected level of service, e.g., LNAV/VNAV or LPV may not be available.  Wide Area Augmentation System (WAAS).

			MissedApproachGroup&Properties of the Missed Approach

MissedApproachGroup-instruction&Operational instructions that must be observed when flying the Missed Approach.
MissedApproachGroup-alternateClimbInstruction&A second climb-to-altitude provided on a missed approach based off the remote altimeter source.  It is provided when the 40:1 surface can not be cleared.  For example, (6,100 when using Denver/Stapleton altimeter setting) is a parenthetical instruction.
MissedApproachGroup-alternateClimbAltitude&The altitude for the alternate climb instruction.  (In PANS-OPS and TERPS design this is the 40:1 surface penetration - second climb to altitude.)

			
			TerminalArrivalArea&The lowest altitude that will provide a minimum clearance of 300 metres (1000 feet) above all objects located in an arc of a circle defined by a 46 kilometre (25 nautical mile) radius centred on the initial approach fix (IAF), or where there is no IAF then centred on the intermediate approach fix (IF), delimited by straight lines joining the extremity of the arc to the IAF/IF.

TerminalArrivalArea-arrivalAreaType&Indicates the base type of the arrival area. Types include:  Left Base, Right Base, Straight In
TerminalArrivalArea-outerBufferWidth&Buffer size of the outer arc boundary
TerminalArrivalArea-lateralBufferWidth&Buffer size of the lateral (or inner) boundary

			TerminalArrivalAreaSector&Subdivision of the TAA to allow for lower altitudes. The lowest altitude will provide a minimum clearance of 300m (1000ft) above all objects located in the sector.

TerminalArrivalAreaSector-flyByCode&Indicates if the aircraft is not required to fly directly over the fix. If code is Yes, then it is a 'flyby' waypoint. If the code is No or nil, then the associated fix is a 'fly-over' waypoint. [ICAO] Waypoints are identified as either flyover or fly-by.
TerminalArrivalAreaSector-procedureTurnRequired&Indicates that a course reversal is not required. If the code is Yes, then the products will indicate 'NoPT'.
TerminalArrivalAreaSector-altitudeDescription&A code indicating how the altitude attributes should be interpreted: 'at' the lower altitude, 'at or above' the lower altitude, 'at or below' the lower altitude or 'between' the altitudes specified in the attributes lowerAltitude and upperAltitude distances.

			
			FASDataBlock&Final Approach Segment Data Block.  The additional information about the Precision Final Segment.  Most attributes describe the LPV path point record required for WAAS procedures.

FASDataBlock-horizontalAlarmLimit&(ARINC) Horizontal Alert Limit (HAL) is the radius of a circle in the horizontal plane (the local plane tangent to the WGS-84 ellipsoid), with its centre being at the true position, which describes the region which is required to contain the indicated horizontal position with the required probability for a particular navigation mode assuming the probability of a GPS satellite integrity failure being included in the position solution is less than or equal to E-4 per hour.
FASDataBlock-verticalAlarmLimit&(ARINC) Vertical Alert Limit (VAL) is half the length of a segment on the vertical axis (perpendicular to the horizontal plane of WGS-84 ellipsoid), with its centre being at the true position, which describes the region which is required to contain the indicated vertical position with a probability of 1-E-7 per approach, assuming the probability of a GPS satellite integrity failure being included in the position solution is less than or equal to E-4 per hour.
FASDataBlock-thresholdCourseWidth&The width of the lateral course at the Landing Threshold Point (LTP). This width, in conjunction with the location of the Flight Path Alignment Point (FPAP) defines the sensitivity of the lateral deviations throughout the approach.
FASDataBlock-lengthOffset&Distance from the stop end of the runway to the Flight Path Alignment Point
FASDataBlock-CRCRemainder&Hexadecimal representation of the 32-bit CRC used to check the integrity of the FAS data block.
FASDataBlock-operationType&Operation Type. A number from 0 to 15 that indicates the type of the final approach segment.
FASDataBlock-serviceProviderSBAS&SBAS Service Provider Identifier. A number from 0 to 15 that associates the ApproachProcedure to a particular satellite based approach system service provider.
FASDataBlock-approachPerformanceDesignator&Approach Performance Designator. A number from 0 to 7 that identifies the type of approach.
FASDataBlock-routeIndicator&Route Indicator. A single alpha character (A through Z or blank, omitting I and O) used to differentiate between multiple final approach segments to the same runway or heliport.
FASDataBlock-referencePathDataSelector&Reference Path Data Selector (RPDS). A number (0-48) that enables automatic tuning of a procedure by LAAS avionics.
FASDataBlock-referencePathIdentifier&Reference Path Identifier. A four-character identifier that is used to confirm selection of the correct ApproachProcedure.
FASDataBlock-codeICAO&The first two designators of the ICAO location identifier, as identified in ICAO Doc 7910.

			
			CirclingArea&[FAA 8260.3] The area in which aircraft circle to land under visual conditions after completing an instrument landing approach.


			CirclingRestriction&Describes a (sub)sector used to restrict flight within a circling area.

			Minima&Vertical and horizontal visual minimums for a procedure segment conditions such as aircraft category, navigation equipment usage, procedure type, altimeter, etc.
