			DepartureArrivalCondition&A condition which is established for a departure or an arrival

DepartureArrivalCondition-minimumEnrouteAltitude&Minimum en-route altitude (MEA). The altitude for an en-route segment that provides adequate reception of relevant navigation facilities and ATS communications, complies with the airspace structure and provides the required obstacle clearance.
DepartureArrivalCondition-minimumCrossingAtEnd&The lowermost vertical position at the end point, when flying on the route portion in the direction indicated in the RoutePortionUsage.
DepartureArrivalCondition-minimumCrossingAtEndReference&The reference surface used for the value of the minimumCrossingAtEnd. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
DepartureArrivalCondition-maximumCrossingAtEnd&The uppermost vertical position at the end point, when flying on the route portion in the direction indicated in the RoutePortionUsage.
DepartureArrivalCondition-maximumCrossingAtEndReference&The reference surface used for the value of the maximumCrossingAtEnd. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..

			NavigationArea&An area specified by sectors with altitude or procedure descent gradient limitations for omnidirectional departures or Pilot navigation area.

NavigationArea-navigationAreaType&Indicates what type of area is defined; omnidirectional area, pilot navigation area.
NavigationArea-minimumCeiling&The minimum cloud base needed when using this departure navigation area.
NavigationArea-minimumVisibility&The minimum visibility needed when using this departure navigation area.

			NavigationAreaSector&Subdivision of a sector to allow for different altitudes or gradients.


			SectorDesign&Design criteria used for the NavigationAreaSector.

SectorDesign-turnDirection&A code indicating the direction of the turn.
SectorDesign-designGradient&Procedure design Gradient 
SectorDesign-terminationAltitude&Termination Altitude
SectorDesign-turnPermitted&Indicates if the sector is clear for the direction of turn.

			StandardInstrumentDeparture&A designated instrument flight rule (IFR) departure route linking the aerodrome or a specific runway of the aerodrome with a specified significant point, normally on a designated ATS route, at which the en-route phase of a flight commences.

StandardInstrumentDeparture-designator&The full textual designator of the SID.
For example, - KOGAL1A - a Standard Instrument Departure ending at a designated point KOGAL.
StandardInstrumentDeparture-contingencyRoute&flag indicating the departure is a contingency route

			
			SafeAltitudeArea&A set of Minimum Sector Altitudes which completely describe an area centred on a significant point, usually contained within a sector of 46km (25NM) radius. 

SafeAltitudeArea-safeAreaType&Indicates the type of area, either MSA or ESA

			SafeAltitudeAreaSector&Subdivision of the MSA to allow for lower altitudes.

SafeAltitudeAreaSector-bufferWidth&Width of the secondary area used to evaluate the lowest usable altitude for obstacle assessment.

			
			ApproachLeg&A portion of a terminal ApproachProcedure as defined by two consecutive significant points. 


			ArrivalFeederLeg&A type of SegmentLeg designed in accordance with the rules for arrival feeder segments having the properties specific to a arrival feeder approach segment.

ArrivalFeederLeg-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.

			ArrivalLeg&A portion of an ArrivalProcedure (STAR) as defined by two consecutive significant points. 

ArrivalLeg-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.

			DepartureLeg&A portion of an DepartureProcedure as defined by two consecutive significant points. 

DepartureLeg-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.
DepartureLeg-minimumObstacleClearanceAltitude&Minimum obstacle clearance altitude (MOCA). The minimum altitude for a defined segment of flight that provides the required obstacle clearance. 

			FinalLeg&A type of SegmentLeg designed in accordance with the rules for final segments having the properties specific to a final approach segment..

FinalLeg-guidanceSystem&Guidance system used on the final approach segment of an instrument ApproachProcedure.  (Commonly used to differentiate lines in a minima table.)
FinalLeg-landingSystemCategory&Landing system category for use of the minima.
FinalLeg-minimumBaroVnavTemperature&[FAA-H-8261-1] The temperature at which a Baro-VNAV is noted NA. It is the minimum temperature limitation published for each procedure for which Baro-VNAV minimums are published. This temperature represents the airport temperature below which the use of Baro-VNAV is not authorized to the LNAV/VNAV DA.

For example, the note Baro-VNAV NA below -20 deg. C (-5 deg. F) implies that the approach may not be flown at all using Baro-VNAV when the temperature is below -20 deg. Celsius. However, Baro-VNAV may be used for approach guidance down to the published LNAV MDA.

Note: Used in the LNAV final segment.
FinalLeg-rnpDMEAuthorized&Applies to RNAVguidance.  Indicates if DME/DME RNP 0.3 is allowed.

DME/DME based RNP-.03 systems may be used only when a chart note indicates DME/DME availability, for example, "DME/DME RNP-0.3 Authorized." Specific DME facilities may be required, for example, "DME/DME RNP-0.3 Authorized, ABC, XYZ required."

Note: Used on RNAV final segment.
FinalLeg-courseOffsetAngle&Final Approach Course Offset Angle. Indicates the offset angle between the final approach course and the extended runway centreline.
FinalLeg-courseOffsetSide&Final Approach Course Offset Side. Indicates on which side of the extended runway centreline that the final approach course lies, when viewed from the Final Approach Fix.
FinalLeg-courseCentrelineDistance&Final Approach Course Centre Line Distance. Indicates the distance from the Landing Threshold Point (LTP) to the point where the extended runway centreline intersects the final approach course.
FinalLeg-courseOffsetDistance&Final Approach Course Offset Distance. Indicates the distance between the final approach course and extended runway centreline at a point located 3000 ft from the Landing Threshold Point (LTP), measured perpendicular to the extended runway centreline
FinalLeg-courseCentrelineIntersect&Indicates if the intersection of the final approach course with the extended runway centreline is located before or after the Landing Threshold Point (LTP).

			HoldingUse&Describes how the holding pattern is used on a segment.

HoldingUse-holdingUse&Indicates how the holding is used on the approach segment.
HoldingUse-instruction&Operational instructions concerning the use of the Holding Pattern in relation with a Procedure.
HoldingUse-instructedAltitude&An altitude referenced in the holding use instructions.
HoldingUse-instructionAltitudeReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.

			InitialLeg&A type of segmentleg designed in accordance with the rules for initial segments having the properties specific to a initial approach segment.

InitialLeg-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.

			IntermediateLeg&A type of SegmentLeg designed in accordance with the rules for intermediate segments having the properties specific to an intermediate approach segment.. The intermediate segment begins at the point where the initial approach intercepts the FAC.

IntermediateLeg-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.

			LandingTakeoffAreaCollection&The grouping of Landing Areas or Takeoff Areas serviced by the procedure.


			MissedApproachLeg&A type of SegmentLeg designed in accordance with the rules for missed approach segments having the properties specific to a missed approach segment.. The missed approach segment begins at DA and ends at the clearance limit.

MissedApproachLeg-type&Indicates if the missed approach leg is part of the primary instruction.
MissedApproachLeg-thresholdAfterMAPT&Indicates if MAP is before or after the Threshold
MissedApproachLeg-heightMAPT&Elevation of the missed approach surface at the missed approach point.
MissedApproachLeg-requiredNavigationPerformance&[ICAO] Required navigation performance (RNP). [ICAO] Specifies the minimum navigation performance accuracy required in an airspace. It is the navigation performance accuracy of all the user and navigation system combinations within an airspace. 

Note: It is a tolerance factor for flying.  The factor is taken into consideration when determining protected airspace for aircraft.

			NavigationAreaRestriction&Areas that are restricted from use for a procedure.  Example is restricted areas defined for an omnidirectional departure.

NavigationAreaRestriction-type&Indicated the type of restriction area

			Procedure&A series of predetermined manoeuvres with specified protection from obstacles.

Procedure-communicationFailureInstruction&Operational instructions which must be observed in case of communication failure.
Procedure-instruction&Some free text to describe operational instructions (other than communication failure instructions) which must be respected when flying the Procedure.
Procedure-designCriteria&Rules used in the design of the procedure.
Procedure-codingStandard&The set of rules followed when encoding the procedure legs
Procedure-flightChecked&Indicates if the procedure has been flight checked.
Procedure-name&The name of the instrument procedure.
Procedure-RNAV&Indicates the procedure is an RNAV procedure

			ProcedureDME&DME facilities that are used for a particular segments for DME/DME navigation.

ProcedureDME-criticalDME&An indication that the DME is critical for navigation on a procedure segment.
ProcedureDME-satisfactory&Specifies whether the critical DME passed satisfactory or unsatisfactory. 

			ProcedureTransition&A group of consecutive segments that are part of a branch  on an ApproachProcedure, SID or STAR.

ProcedureTransition-transitionId&Used strictly for ARINC coding.  The identifier will be the initial point for each transition.  A transition includes multiple SegmentLegs.  
ProcedureTransition-type&The type of transition.
ProcedureTransition-instruction&Operational instructions that must be observed when flying the ProcedureTransition part.
ProcedureTransition-vectorHeading&A heading provided for use, when a departure is designed to incorporate radar vectors at the termination point,  in the event ATC instructions are not received prior to or at the termination fix.

			ProcedureTransitionLeg&Characterises a SegmentLeg which is part of a Procedure Transition

ProcedureTransitionLeg-seqNumberARINC&Indicates the order of the SegmentLegs within a transition.

			SegmentLeg&A portion of a procedure as defined by two consecutive significant points. 

SegmentLeg-endConditionDesignator&An indication of the event that allows identifying the end of the leg and the start of the next leg on the procedure.  For example, reaching an altitude or outbound timing.
SegmentLeg-legPath&A code defining a specific type of flight path such as arc, base turn outbound, base turn inbound, track, proc turn, hold in lieu.
SegmentLeg-legTypeARINC&A comprehensive description of the 'path and terminator' concept is given in ARINC Specification 424, Attachment 5, Path and Terminator. 
SegmentLeg-course&The value of the course angle in degrees.
SegmentLeg-courseType&A code indicating the type of course to be observed. E.g. true track, magnetic track, heading, VOR radial, true bearing, magnetic bearing.
SegmentLeg-courseDirection&Indicates flight direction to/from the navaid providing the course guidance.
SegmentLeg-turnDirection&A code indicating the direction of the turn.
SegmentLeg-speedLimit&The value of the speed limit on the procedure leg.  

Rules: 
As a plausibility rule, value should be equivalent to between 0 and 400, when expressed in Km/h.
SegmentLeg-speedReference&A code indicating the reference system for a speed value.
SegmentLeg-speedInterpretation&A code indicating how the speed attributes of a procedure leg should be interpreted.
SegmentLeg-bankAngle&The recommended bank angle of the aircraft on the turn.  

Rules: 
As a plausibility rule, value should be between 5 and 35 degrees.
SegmentLeg-length&Length of the segment
SegmentLeg-duration&Segment duration
SegmentLeg-procedureTurnRequired&Indicates if a procedure turn is required at the end of the segmentleg.  Default is No.
SegmentLeg-upperLimitAltitude&The value of the upper altitude
used with codeDescrDistVer:
At or below the higher altitude.
Between the lower and the upper altitude.
SegmentLeg-upperLimitReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
SegmentLeg-lowerLimitAltitude&The lower limit altitude.  

used with codeDescrDistVer:
At or above the lower altitude.
At the lower altitude
Between the lower and the upper altitude.
Lower altitude is recommended.
Expect lower altitude by ATC.
SegmentLeg-lowerLimitReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
SegmentLeg-altitudeInterpretation&A code indicating how the altitude attributes of a procedure leg should be interpreted.
SegmentLeg-altitudeOverrideATC&Alternate altitude when directed by Air Traffic Control
SegmentLeg-altitudeOverrideReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
SegmentLeg-verticalAngle&The value of the vertical climb angle of the aircraft on the procedure leg. A negative value means descent.

Rules: 
As a plausibility rule, value should be between -10 and +50 degrees.

			
			ProcedureAvailability&Information about the status of the procedure for flight planning/operations.

ProcedureAvailability-status&A code indicating the status of the procedure for flight planning/operations.

			
			
			ChangeOverPoint&The distance from the start of the route portion to the position where change over occurs for VOR defined routes.

ChangeOverPoint-distance&The distance from the start of the route portion to position of the change over point.

			Route&A specified route designed for channelling the flow of traffic as necessary for the provision of air traffic services, from the end of the take-off and initial climb phase to the commencement of the approach and landing phase.

Route-designatorPrefix&A prefix for the route designator, indicating whether the route is upper ATS, reserved for helicopters or reserved for supersonic flights.
Route-designatorSecondLetter&The letter of the route designator. Depending on the region, letters may have special significance with regard to the route usage limitations.
Route-designatorNumber&The number of the route designator.
Route-multipleIdentifier&A suffix for the route designator, indicating alternates for homonymous routes (especially for military training routes).
Route-locationDesignator&A textual description of the area in which a designated route is situated.
Route-name&A free text name by which the route is known.
Route-type&Route classification.
Route-flightRule&A code indicating the flight rules to be observed by aircraft.
For example, VFR and/or IFR.
Route-internationalUse&A code indicating if the route segment is international or domestic.
Route-militaryUse&A code indicating whether the route is for exclusive use by military aircraft.
Route-militaryTrainingType&A code indicating the type of military training activity for which the route has been designed.

			RouteAvailability&Information about the operational availability of a route.

RouteAvailability-direction&A code indicating the direction in which the route segment is considered when a specific usage is described, ie. forward or backward.
RouteAvailability-cardinalDirection&The direction for which the usage is specified, expressed as compass angle.
RouteAvailability-status&The availability status of the route, in the direction indicated by the direction and/or cardinalDirection attribute.

			RouteDME&DME facilities that are used for a particular route for DME/DME navigation.

RouteDME-criticalDME&An indication that the DME is critical for navigation on the route portion.
RouteDME-satisfactory&Specifies whether the critical DME passed satisfactory or unsatisfactory. 

			RoutePortion&A group of two or more consecutive segments of the same route, which have the usage and/or the same FlightRestrictions.


			RouteSegment&A portion of a route to be flown usually without an intermediate stop, as defined by two consecutive significant points.

RouteSegment-level&A code indicating if the route segment is in the upper airspace, the lower airspace or both.
RouteSegment-upperLimit&The vertical position of the route segment ceiling.
RouteSegment-upperLimitReference&The reference surface used for the value of the upper limit. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
RouteSegment-lowerLimit&The vertical position of the route segment floor.
RouteSegment-lowerLimitReference&The reference surface used for the value of the lower limit. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
RouteSegment-minimumObstacleClearanceAltitude&Minimum obstacle clearance altitude (MOCA). The minimum altitude for a defined segment of flight that provides the required obstacle clearance. 
RouteSegment-pathType&The type of segment path.
For example, great circle, rhumbline, geodesic line, etc.
RouteSegment-trueTrack&The initial true track.
RouteSegment-magneticTrack&The initial magnetic track.
RouteSegment-reverseTrueTrack&The reverse initial true track.
RouteSegment-reverseMagneticTrack&The reverse initial magnetic track.
RouteSegment-length&The length of the path (depending on the type of the path).
RouteSegment-widthLeft&The distance from the centreline of the route segment to the left edge, when considering the direction from the start point to the end point.
RouteSegment-widthRight&The distance from the centreline of the route segment to the right edge, when considering the direction from the start point to the end point.
RouteSegment-turnDirection&Indicates the turn direction (if any) at the end of the current segment, in order to continue on to the next segment of the same route.
RouteSegment-signalGap&indicates a signal gap in the segment
RouteSegment-minimumEnrouteAltitude&Minimum en-route altitude (MEA). The altitude for an en-route segment that provides adequate reception of relevant navigation facilities and ATS communications, complies with the airspace structure and provides the required obstacle clearance.
RouteSegment-minimumCrossingAtEnd&The lowermost vertical position at the end point, when flying on the route portion in the direction indicated in the RoutePortionUsage.
RouteSegment-minimumCrossingAtEndReference&The reference surface used for the value of the minimumCrossingAtEnd. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
RouteSegment-maximumCrossingAtEnd&The uppermost vertical position at the end point, when flying on the route portion in the direction indicated in the RoutePortionUsage.
RouteSegment-maximumCrossingAtEndReference&The reference surface used for the value of the maximumCrossingAtEnd. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
RouteSegment-navigationType&Classification of the Route Portion for navigational purposes. Examples: conventional, RNAV.
RouteSegment-requiredNavigationPerformance&A code indicating the required navigation performance for the route portion
RouteSegment-designatorSuffix&A suffix for the route designator (according ICAO Annex 11), indicating whether advisory service only is available on that portion, or the RNP status of the route portion.

			
			AirspaceBorderCrossing&A type of traffic flow condition element which consist of crossing the common border between two adjacent airspace, when flying directly from one airspace into the other airspace.


			DirectFlight&A direct flight (DCT) between two significant points, outside the existing route network.


			DirectFlightClass&A category of direct flights (DCT), having some particular characteristics, such as a minimum length.

DirectFlightClass-exceedLength&A value used to indicate that only Direct Flights (DCT) that exceed this value are concerned.

			DirectFlightSegment&A direct flight (DCT) between two specified significant points.


			FlightConditionCircumstance&Circumstance related to the elementary condition (such as departing from an aerodrome),  which is used to further refine the  selection of flights being affected by the restriction.

FlightConditionCircumstance-referenceLocation&A code indicating if the condition element is a reference location for the flight restriction, i.e. if the time schedule associated with the restriction must be considered as applicable for that flight condition element.
FlightConditionCircumstance-relationWithLocation&A code qualifying a location (such as an airspace, aerodrome, point, etc.) when used as condition element. For example, departing from that location, crossing the location, activation hours of the location are used as condition, etc..

			FlightConditionCombination&A combination of conditions involving:
1) an operator such as \"AND\", \"OR\", \"AND NOT\", \"SEQUENCE\", \"NONE\" and
2) one or more operands, each of these being either a condition element or another combination of conditions.

FlightConditionCombination-logicalOperator&The type of operation combining an elementary condition or a previously defined combination with other elementary conditions or previously defined combinations.

			FlightConditionElement&An operand in a flight condition combination.

FlightConditionElement-index&A sequence number used to indicate the order of the operand when composing the FlightConditionCombination.

			FlightConditionElementChoice&A link class that allows selecting between an elementary condition and a preceding combination of conditions, to be used as operand in a subsequent combination of flight conditions


			FlightRestriction&A rule meant to regulate the use of the route network, by identifying a set of flights which fulfil a combination of elementary flow conditions and either forbidding them on a particular routing or obliging them to follow one routing out of a set of mandatory alternatives.

FlightRestriction-designator&A coded value which identifies the restriction.
FlightRestriction-type&A code indicating if the restriction is an interdiction or a mandatory routing.
FlightRestriction-instruction&Some free text to describe the operational instructions which form the FlightRestriction.

			FlightRestrictionLevel&A single level or a level band associated with a flight restriction, either condition or routing element.

FlightRestrictionLevel-upperLevel&The value of the uppermost cruising level.
The data type also allows a special non-numerical value "CEILING", meaning "the top of the airspace. This can useful in the case of Airspace that have a non-constant upper limit.
FlightRestrictionLevel-upperLevelReference&The reference surface used for the value of the upper level. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
FlightRestrictionLevel-lowerLevel&The value of the lowermost cruising level.
The data type also allows a special non-numerical value "FLOOR" meaning "the bottom of the airspace".  This can useful in the case of Airspace that have a non-constant lower limit.
FlightRestrictionLevel-lowerLevelReference&The reference surface used for the value of the lower level. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..

			FlightRestrictionRoute&A sequence of routing elements (points, route portions or airspace) that must/must not appear in the specified order in the flight plan of an aircraft fulfilling the conditions of the related Flight Restriction (according to its type attribute).

FlightRestrictionRoute-priorPermission&The minimum lead time required for contacting the relevant authority in order to get permission for using the routing.

			FlightRoutingElement&An airspace, route or point that is concerned by a specified flight restriction.

FlightRoutingElement-orderNumber&A number in sequence used to indicate the order of the routing element in the flight restriction routing to which it belongs.
FlightRoutingElement-speed&The value of the speed limit imposed on a routing element.
FlightRoutingElement-speedReference&A code indicating the reference system for the speed value. For example: IAS, TAS or GS (ground speed).
FlightRoutingElement-speedCriteria&A code indicating whether the speed is a maximum, a minimum or an imposed value.

			FlightRoutingElementChoice&A link class that allows selecting between an AirportHeliport, an airspace, a fix, a procedure or an AerialRefuelling which is impacted by a flight restriction


			
			RulesProcedures&The definition of an instruction or regulation that needs to be considered by personnel involved in flight operations in relation with an airport/heliport or an airspace.

RulesProcedures-category&An indication of the purpose of the rule or procedure
RulesProcedures-title&A general heading by which the rule or procedure is usually identified in the Aeronautical Information Publications (AIP) or similar/related documents.
RulesProcedures-content&The definition of the actual content of the rule or procedure

			
			AirTrafficControlService&A kind of service that provides control and separation services to aircraft in the air.

AirTrafficControlService-type&The type of air traffic control service provided.

			AirTrafficManagementService&A kind of service that provides flight planning and flow management operations.

AirTrafficManagementService-type&The type of air traffic flow management service provided.

			AircraftGroundService&A kind of maintenance, support or supply service provided to aircraft at the ground.

Note: instances should be grouped by provider (associated Unit)

AircraftGroundService-type&The type of ground service.

			AirportClearanceService&A kind of service that provides clearance capabilities for airport surfaces.

AirportClearanceService-snowPlan&Description of the snow removal priorities.

			AirportGroundService&Services that provide maintenance of the airport infrastructure and direct support to aircraft on the ground.


			AirportSuppliesService&A kind of service that provides supplies (fuel, oil, oxygen, etc.) to aircraft.

Note: instances should be grouped by provider (associated Unit)


			CallsignDetail&Information about the operational identifier by which the provider of the service is called and the language used.

CallsignDetail-callSign&The full textual service provider identification or call-sign for a particular frequency.
For example, Athinai Control, Malmoe Radar, etc..
CallsignDetail-language&A code indicating the language in which the service is provided on a particular frequency, as associated with a particular call-sign. 

			FireFightingService&A kind of airport service that provides rescue and fire fighting capabilities for aircraft in emergency at and around the airport.

FireFightingService-category&A standard categorisation of the rescue and fire-fighting capabilities of an aerodrome on the basis of the length and fuselage width of the largest aircraft to be rescued.
FireFightingService-standard&A code indicating the standard referred to by the fire fighting category value.

			Fuel&Fuel types used for aircraft/helicopters.

Fuel-category&A code indicating a type of fuel for aircraft and helicopters (e.g. OCT73, OCT80-87, AVGAS, OCT100-130, OCT115-145, MOGAS, JET, A1, A1+, B, JP4, JP5).

			GroundTrafficControlService&A kind of service that provides control and separation services, to aircraft at the airport.

GroundTrafficControlService-type&The type of ground traffic control service provided.

			InformationService&A kind of service that consists in the provision of aeronautical, meteorological, traffic and related information to aircraft crew and other actors involved in flight operations, in flight or on the ground.

InformationService-type&The type of information service provided.
InformationService-voice&Indicating whether the service is provided as voice message.
InformationService-dataLink&Indicates whether the service is available via data-link.
InformationService-recorded&Indicates that the information broadcast is recorded and played back rather than a live transmission.

			Nitrogen&NITROGEN supplies in aviation.

Nitrogen-type&The type of nitrogen supplies for aviation usage.

			Oil&Oil types used for aircraft/helicopters.

Oil-category&A code indicating a category of oil used in aircraft (e.g. TURBO, AVIA, HYD).

			Oxygen&Oxygen supplies used in aviation.

Oxygen-type&The type of oxygen supplies for aviation usage.

			PassengerService&Passenger services and facilities available at an aerodrome/heliport (like medical facilities) or in the surrounding area (hotels in city etc.).

PassengerService-type&A code indicating the type of passenger facility/service available.

			PilotControlledLighting&Service providing airborne control of lights by keying the aircraft's microphone.  Often available at locations without specified hours for lighting and where there is no control tower or Flight Service Station (FSS);  or when the tower or FSS is closed (locations with part-time tower or FSS).

PilotControlledLighting-type&Type of pilot controlled lighting service - standard or non-standard.
PilotControlledLighting-duration&The length of time the lighting is illuminated, normally 15 minutes.
PilotControlledLighting-intensitySteps&The number of intensity steps/levels for a particular type of lighting system.
PilotControlledLighting-standByIntensity&The intensity step/level of the lighting system when not in use.
PilotControlledLighting-radioFrequency&The radio frequency to be used by the pilot for the activation of the system.
PilotControlledLighting-activationInstruction&Operational instructions for controlling the lighting systems.

			RadioCommunicationChannel&A radio frequency band of sufficient width and associated identification data used for one- or two-way communication from or to a transmitter on the ground or in the air.

RadioCommunicationChannel-mode&The type of communication channel.
RadioCommunicationChannel-rank&A code indicating the role of the communication channel, in terms of primary, alternate, emergency, etc.
RadioCommunicationChannel-frequencyTransmission&The value of the transmission frequency.
RadioCommunicationChannel-frequencyReception&The value of the reception frequency.
RadioCommunicationChannel-channel&The identifier of the radio channel on which the communication takes place.
RadioCommunicationChannel-logon&A specified code used for data link, such as used for logon to an ATS unit.
RadioCommunicationChannel-emissionType&A code indicating the type of emission, as defined at the 1979 ITU World Administrative Radio Conference.
For example, A3E, etc..
RadioCommunicationChannel-selectiveCall&A code indicating if whether or not a frequency treats "selective call".
RadioCommunicationChannel-flightChecked&Indicates if the communication channel has been flight checked.
RadioCommunicationChannel-trafficDirection&Indicates the eventual directionality of the communication channel.

			RadioCommunicationOperationalStatus&Radio communication channel operational status information.

RadioCommunicationOperationalStatus-operationalStatus&Indicates the operational capability of the operational channel.

			SearchRescueService&The performance of distress monitoring, communication, coordination and search and rescue functions, initial medical assistance or medical evacuation, through the use of public and private resources, including cooperating aircraft, vessels and other craft and installations.

SearchRescueService-type&The type of air traffic flow management service provided.

			Service&The provision of tangible goods, information, instructions, guidance, etc. to pilots, flights, aircraft operators and other personnel and institutions concerned with flight operations.

Service-flightOperations&The destination (arriving, departing, etc.) of the flights for which the information is provided.
Service-rank&The order of priority of the service, such as "primary" or "alternate".
Service-compliantICAO&A code indicating whether the service is compliant with the ICAO standards and recommended practices specified for this type of service.
Service-name&A free text name by which the service is identified.

			ServiceOperationalStatus&Service operational status.

ServiceOperationalStatus-operationalStatus&Indicates the operational capability of the service.

			TrafficSeparationService&A kind of service that provides control and separation services, to aircraft in the air and on the ground.

TrafficSeparationService-radarAssisted&A code indicating if the service is provided with radar assistance.
TrafficSeparationService-dataLinkEnabled&Indicates if Controller-Pilot Data-Link Communication (CPDLC) is available in support of the service.
TrafficSeparationService-dataLinkChannel&The channel on which the data-link takes place, if applicable. 

			
			
			ContactInformation&Information required to enable contact with the responsible person and/or organisation.  This model is derived from ISO19115-2003:Geographic Information- Metadata

ContactInformation-name&The official name of the contact.
ContactInformation-title&The official title of the contact.

			OnlineContact&On-line or Network information that can be used to contact the individual or organisation, including eMail address and web site page.

OnlineContact-network&The official name telecommunication network on which the resource is located. 
OnlineContact-linkage&Location (address) for on-line access using a Uniform Resource Locator address or similar addressing scheme such as http://www.statkart.no/isotc211
OnlineContact-protocol&The connection protocol to be used.
OnlineContact-eMail&The address of the electronic mailbox of the responsible organisation or individual.

			PostalAddress&Physical address at which the organization or individual may be contacted. Derived from ISO19115-2003

PostalAddress-deliveryPoint&The street address line for the location.  More than one address line may be used.
PostalAddress-city&The city of the location or organisation.
PostalAddress-administrativeArea&The state or province of the location or organisation.
PostalAddress-postalCode&The ZIP or other postal code for the location or organisation.
PostalAddress-country&The country of the physical address for the location or organisation. Full name, not ISO 3166 abbreviations.

			TelephoneContact&Telephone numbers at which the organisation or individual may be contacted.  From ISO19115-2003

TelephoneContact-voice&The telephone number by which individuals can speak to the responsible organisation or individual.
TelephoneContact-facsimile&The telephone number of a facsimile machine for the responsible organisation or individual.

			
			AircraftCharacteristic&A specific aircraft type, such as airplane, balloon, helicopter, etc., and/or having specific equipment (certification), such as RNAV or RVSM.

AircraftCharacteristic-type&Indicating the type of an aircraft.
AircraftCharacteristic-engine&Indicating the type of aircraft engine.
AircraftCharacteristic-numberEngine&A coded indication for the number of engines of an aircraft.
AircraftCharacteristic-typeAircraftICAO&A coded aircraft type designator assigned by ICAO to all aircraft heavier than micro-/ultra-light.
AircraftCharacteristic-aircraftLandingCategory&Classification of aircraft based on 1.3 times stall speed in landing configuration at maximum certified landing mass.
AircraftCharacteristic-wingSpan&The distance between the wing tips of the aircraft.
AircraftCharacteristic-wingSpanInterpretation&Indicates whether the Aircraft Characteristic concerns aircraft with larger or smaller wingspan.
AircraftCharacteristic-classWingSpan&A classification of aircraft by wing span dimensions.  It can be used to indicate the size of aircraft that a taxiway can handle.
AircraftCharacteristic-weight&The maximum aircraft take-off weight.
AircraftCharacteristic-weightInterpretation&Indicates whether the Aircraft Characteristic concerns aircraft with bigger or smaller weight.
AircraftCharacteristic-passengers&The maximum number of passengers
AircraftCharacteristic-passengersInterpretation&Indicates whether the Aircraft Characteristic concerns aircraft with larger or smaller number of passengers.
AircraftCharacteristic-speed&A speed (IAS) that can be maintained by the aircraft.
AircraftCharacteristic-speedInterpretation&Indicates whether the speed is a maximum or minimum imposed value.
AircraftCharacteristic-wakeTurbulence&The wake turbulence category of the aircraft.
AircraftCharacteristic-navigationEquipment&An indication of the aircraft capability to use a certain ground based, satellite based or on-board system for aerial navigation.
AircraftCharacteristic-navigationSpecification&A set of AircraftAndFlight crew requirements needed to support performance-based navigation operations.
AircraftCharacteristic-verticalSeparationCapability&An indication of the aircraft capability to maintain a specified vertical separation.
AircraftCharacteristic-antiCollisionAndSeparationEquipment&An indication of the aircraft equipment with collision avoidance systems.
AircraftCharacteristic-communicationEquipment&An indication of the aircraft equipment with voice and data communication devices.
AircraftCharacteristic-surveillanceEquipment&An indication of the aircraft capability for operating with a certain surveillance system.

			FlightCharacteristic&A specific flight type, such as IFR/VFR, national/international, OAT/GAT, etc.

FlightCharacteristic-type&A code indicating a specified  type of a flight, such as OAT/GAT.
FlightCharacteristic-rule&A code indicating a specific flight rule, such as IFR or VFR.
FlightCharacteristic-status&The designation of a special status for a flight (e.g. ""HEAD"" for Head of State, ""STATE"" for State aircraft other than that of the Head of State).
FlightCharacteristic-military&A code indicating whether it is a military flight.
FlightCharacteristic-origin&A code indicating the origin of the flight with regard to the national borders.
FlightCharacteristic-purpose&A code indicating the purpose of the flight.

			
			AirspaceLayer&The portion of airspace between two specified vertical levels.

AirspaceLayer-upperLimit&Upper limit of the block. 
The data type also allows a special non-numerical value "CEILING", meaning "the top of the airspace. This can useful in the case of Airspace that have a non-constant upper limit.
AirspaceLayer-upperLimitReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
AirspaceLayer-lowerLimit&Lower limit of the block.
The data type also allows a special non-numerical value "FLOOR" meaning "the bottom of the airspace".  This can useful in the case of Airspace that have a non-constant lower limit.
AirspaceLayer-lowerLimitReference&A code indicating the reference for a vertical distance.
Two series of values exist:
1) real distance: from GND, from the MSL, from the WGS-84 ellipsoid
2) pressure distance: QFE, QNH, STD.
AirspaceLayer-altitudeInterpretation&Indicates how the upper and/or lower altitude values should be interpreted.

			
			CircleSector&A group of properties that help describe a 3D pattern based on start angle, stop angle, inner distance, outer distance and upper/lower altitude.

CircleSector-arcDirection&Direction indicating clock-wise or counter-clockwise
CircleSector-fromAngle&Beginning of angle
CircleSector-toAngle&Ending of angle
CircleSector-angleType&A code indicating the type of angle: magnetic, bearing, VOR radial.
CircleSector-angleDirectionReference&A code indicating a direction with regard to a reference point.
CircleSector-innerDistance&Angle sector volume inner limit
CircleSector-outerDistance&Angle sector volume outer limit
CircleSector-upperLimit&The uppermost altitude or level that is included in the sector.
CircleSector-upperLimitReference&The reference surface used for the value of the upper limit. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc..
CircleSector-lowerLimit&The lowermost altitude or level that is included in the sector.
CircleSector-lowerLimitReference&The reference surface used for the value of the lower limit. For example, Mean Sea Level, Ground, standard pressure,  etc.

			EquipmentChoice&A link class that allows selecting between a radio communication channel, a navigational aid, a radar system or a special navigation station which is impacted by the RadioFrequencyArea limitation


			RadioFrequencyArea&A limitation, such as coverage, usability, etc., of a navaid equipment or service frequency

RadioFrequencyArea-type&A code indicating the type of radio navigation aid limitation.

			PropertiesWithSchedule&An abstract class that is used for associating a group of feature properties with a repetitive time period, occurring cyclically inside the validity of the Feature Timeslice, during which these properties have specific values.


			SpecialDate&A calendar date that has a special meaning for a particular State/organisation and which may be referred to in the description of the schedules associated with various aeronautical features.

SpecialDate-type&An indication of the kind of the special dates.
SpecialDate-dateDay&The calendar date concerned.
SpecialDate-dateYear&The year concerned. If no year is indicated, then the same date will be concerned every year.
SpecialDate-name&The name by which the date is known by the public (especially for public holidays).

			Timesheet&The definition of a single time interval, that occurs repeatedly as part of a schedule.

Timesheet-timeReference&A code indicating the time reference system (for example, 'UTC').
Timesheet-startDate&The start date of the validity of a timesheet. Used together with "endDate" to express repetitive time periods like 15 May to 15 November.
Timesheet-endDate&The end date of the validity of a timesheet. Used together with "startDate" to express repetitive time periods like 15 May to 15 November.
Timesheet-day&A code indicating the day the timesheet is referring to.
Timesheet-dayTil&A code indicating the days affected by a timesheet, as follows:
- if the value of this attribute is left blank, the "endTime", "endEvent", "endTimeRelativeEvent" and "endEventInterpretation" properties must be considered as occurring on the day specified in the attribute "day" (e.g. MON from 07:30 till 16:00);
- if the value of this attribute is not blank, the "endTime", "endEvent", "endTimeRelativeEvent" and "endEventInterpretation" properties must be considered as occurring on the day specified in this attribute and the period described by the timesheet is considered to be a continuous one (e.g. MON 07:30 till FRI 16:00);
Timesheet-startTime&The time of the day (specified in the "day" attribute) when the period described in the timesheet starts.
Timesheet-startEvent&A coded reference to an event (like sunset or sunrise), the occurrence of which indicates when the period described in the Timesheet starts.
Timesheet-startTimeRelativeEvent&The number of minutes before or after the event referred to in the "startEvent" attribute when the period described in the Timesheet starts.
Timesheet-startEventInterpretation&When both the "startTime" and "startEvent" values are not blank, this attribute explains how the combination of the two attributes should be interpreted, i.e. which of the two moments in time is the beginning of the period described by the timesheet.
Timesheet-endTime&The time of the day when the period described in the timesheet ends.
Timesheet-endEvent&A coded reference to an event (like sunset or sunrise), the occurrence of which indicates when the period described in the Timesheet ends.
Timesheet-endTimeRelativeEvent&The number of minutes before or after the event referred to in the "endEvent" attribute when the period described in the Timesheet ends.
Timesheet-endEventInterpretation&When both the "endTime" and "endEvent" values are not blank, this attribute explains how the combination of the two attributes should be interpreted, i.e. which of the two moments in time is the end of the period described by the timesheet.
Timesheet-daylightSavingAdjust&Indicates that the startTime and endTime values have to be decreased by one hour when Daylight Saving is in force (summer time).
Timesheet-excluded&Indicates that the time block indicated by the current Timesheet is excluded (subtracted) from the total schedule.

			
			StandardLevel&A specified cruising level, part of a column within a table of discrete cruising levels used by General Air Traffic.

			StandardLevelTable&A table of consecutive cruising levels described under vertical separation criteria limited by an upper and lower level and used by General Air Traffic.

			ObstacleAssessmentArea&The geometry of surfaces used to define the altitude the length of a segment, holding pattern, etc., in function of the obstructions located in the area.

ObstacleAssessmentArea-type&Indicated the type of area being assessed  such as 40:1, 72:1, MA, Final, etc

			ObstaclePlacement&Provides the location relative to

			Obstruction&[FAA 8260.3] The highest airspace, obstacle or terrain relative to a prescribed plane within a specified area.

NOTE: In precision ApproachProcedures where obstacles penetrate the approach surface, the controlling obstacle is the one which results in the requirement for the highest decision height (DH).

Obstruction-requiredClearance&Required altitude adjustment above any obstacle or terrain within a defined safety buffer region. The safety buffer allows for errors in the air and in the accuracy of data such as obstacle accuracy.  This together with other adjustments (human factor adjustments, lighting adjustments, altimeter adjustments, etc). give the minimum altitude.
Obstruction-minimumAltitude&The value of the minimum obstacle clearance altitude. 
Obstruction-surfacePenetration&A code indicating whether the controlling obstacle penetrates the assessment surfaces. Rule: if surfacePenetration is "NO", then slopePenetration will not have a value.
Obstruction-slopePenetration&A value calculated by dividing 102.0 (a constant) with the angle of the glidepath
Obstruction-controlling&Indication whether it is a "controlling obstruction" for the associated ObstacleAssessmentArea.
Obstruction-closeIn&"Close-In Obstacles" are those that would penetrate the 40:1 OCS and would require a climb gradient to 200 feet or less above the departure end of runway.   So if an aircraft climbs at the minimum standard 200 feet per NM, "Close-In Obstacles" are those within 1 NM from the end of the runway.

			SecondarySurveillanceRadar&Secondary Surveillance Radar (SSR aka Secondary Radar (SECRA)) is a radar system in which the object to be detected is fitted with the cooperative equipment in the form of a radio receiver/transmitter (transponder).  Radar pulses transmitted from the searching transmitter/receiver (interrogator) site are received in the cooperative equipment and used to trigger a distinctive transmission from the transponder.  This reply transmission, rather than a reflected signal, is then received back at the transmitter/receiver site for processing and display at an air traffic control facility.

SecondarySurveillanceRadar-transponder&Mode S, or mode select, despite also being called a transponder radar system replacement for Air Traffic Control Radar Beacon System (ATCRBS), is actually a data packet protocol which can be used to augment ATCRBS transponder positioning equipment (radar and TCAS). Mode S is designed to fully interface with ATCRBS systems: mode S SSRs can interrogate ATCRBS transponders, and AIS-P transponders will also reply to older ATCRBS and TCAS interrogations.
SecondarySurveillanceRadar-autonomous&Indicates the SRR is autonomous or independent.
SecondarySurveillanceRadar-monopulse&Monopulse radar is an adaptation of conical scanning radar which sends additional information in the radar signal in order to avoid problems caused by rapid changes in signal strength. The system also makes jamming more difficult. Most radars designed since the 1960s are monopulse systems.

SurveillanceRadar-automatedRadarTerminalSystem&The Automated Radar Terminal System (ARTS) is a system in the air traffic control system using radar intelligence to detect and display pertinent data such as flight identification, altitude, and position of aircraft operating in the terminal area.

A Radar with this attribute automatically tracks controlled aircraft and presents alpha-numeric information adjacent to their targets. It may even automatically calculate the separation between different aircrafts and provide an alert if that separation is compromised as per the set standards.
